            <script>
        /*!
loadCSS: load a CSS file asynchronously.
[c]2014 @scottjehl, Filament Group, Inc.
Licensed MIT
*/
function loadCSS( href, before, media, callback ){
    "use strict";
    // Arguments explained:
    // `href` is the URL for your CSS file.
    // `before` optionally defines the element we'll use as a reference for injecting our <link>
    // By default, `before` uses the first <script> element in the page.
    // However, since the order in which stylesheets are referenced matters, you might need a more specific location in your document.
    // If so, pass a different reference element to the `before` argument and it'll insert before that instead
    // note: `insertBefore` is used instead of `appendChild`, for safety re: http://www.paulirish.com/2011/surefire-dom-element-insertion/
    var ss = window.document.createElement( "link" );
    var ref = before || window.document.getElementsByTagName( "script" )[ 0 ];
    var sheets = window.document.styleSheets;
    ss.rel = "stylesheet";
    ss.href = href;
    // temporarily, set media to something non-matching to ensure it'll fetch without blocking render
    ss.media = "only x";
    // DEPRECATED
    if( callback ) {
        ss.onload = callback;
    }

    // inject link
    ref.parentNode.insertBefore( ss, ref );
    // This function sets the link's media back to `all` so that the stylesheet applies once it loads
    // It is designed to poll until document.styleSheets includes the new sheet.
    ss.onloadcssdefined = function( cb ){
        var defined;
        for( var i = 0; i < sheets.length; i++ ){
            if( sheets[ i ].href && sheets[ i ].href.indexOf( href ) > -1 ){
                defined = true;
            }
        }
        if( defined ){
            cb();
        } else {
            setTimeout(function() {
                ss.onloadcssdefined( cb );
            });
        }
    };
    ss.onloadcssdefined(function() {
        ss.media = media || "all";
    });
    return ss;
}
    </script>

    <p class="petite-text secondary-text mtn">

        <span class="author__name coupled">
            By
            <!--
             - Author Name[, Title]
             -->
                            <a class="secondary-text coupled"
                 href="/high-school/author/michael-florek"
                 rel="author">
                            Michael Florek            </a>, Staff Writer        </span>

                    <!--
             - Author Social Links
             -->
            <small class="article__author__social / minion-text coupled">
                <span class="is-hidden">Contact Michael Florek</span>
                
                    <!--
                     - Twitter Handle
                     -->
                    <span class="is-hidden">on Twitter:</span>
                    <a class="author__social author__social--twitter /
                              solo-icon--twitter-navyBlue10 /
                              coupled secondary-text"
                     href="https://twitter.com/michaelflorek"
                     target="_blank">@michaelflorek</a>
                                            </small>
            </p>
</footer>
                                <!--
                                 - Basic Content
                                 -->
                                <div class="wysiwyg article-content article-content--text tertia-text--long">
    <p><i><b>Editor's note:</b> This story has been updated since it was originally published.</i></p><p>CYPRESS -- Euless Trinity's Mack Beggs is a state champion in a division he doesn't want to be in.&nbsp;</p><p>Beggs, a 17-year-old transgender wrestler from Euless Trinity transitioning from female to male, defeated Katy Morton Ranch's Chelsea Sanchez by major decision, 12-2, to capture the Class 6A 110-pound girls state championship match Saturday evening.&nbsp;</p><p>Before the championship round the&nbsp;PA announcer told the crowd not to take part in action that would cause any wrestler to "doubt their accomplishments this weekend." Beggs took part in the parade of all the state finalists, with his hood up and headphones on most of the time.</p><p>When Beggs' name was announced as a finalist, a large cheer rose up. It was followed by a small amount of boos. Beggs' win was met by an extended cheer mixed with some boos.&nbsp;</p><p>Beggs' victory helped Trinity finish second in the team standings.&nbsp;</p></div>
                                                    
                                            
                            <!--
                             - Images
                             -->
                                                                                                                                    <div class="article-content has-floating-figure tertia-text--long">

                                    <!--
                                     - Figure
                                     -->
                                    <figure class="article-content__figure  figure--right mtn">
    <img class="article-content__figure__img gl-full gm-full gs-full  new-line lazyload"
     data-srcset="https://sportsdaydfw.imgix.net/1488069505-NS_25TRINITYBEGGSFINAL_55574717.JPG?q=50&auto=format&w=300 300w,
                  https://sportsdaydfw.imgix.net/1488069505-NS_25TRINITYBEGGSFINAL_55574717.JPG?q=50&auto=format&w=400 400w,
                  https://sportsdaydfw.imgix.net/1488069505-NS_25TRINITYBEGGSFINAL_55574717.JPG?q=50&auto=format&w=500 500w,
                  https://sportsdaydfw.imgix.net/1488069505-NS_25TRINITYBEGGSFINAL_55574717.JPG?q=50&auto=format&w=600 600w,
                  https://sportsdaydfw.imgix.net/1488069505-NS_25TRINITYBEGGSFINAL_55574717.JPG?q=50&auto=format&w=700 700w,
                  https://sportsdaydfw.imgix.net/1488069505-NS_25TRINITYBEGGSFINAL_55574717.JPG?q=50&auto=format&w=800 800w,
                  https://sportsdaydfw.imgix.net/1488069505-NS_25TRINITYBEGGSFINAL_55574717.JPG?q=50&auto=format&w=900 900w"
          alt="Euless Trinity's Mack Beggs reacts to winning the state championship title in the girls Class 6A girls 110 weight class during the UIL Wrestling State Tournament at Berry Center in Cypress on Saturday, February 25, 2017. Beggs, a 17-year-old transgender wrestler from Euless Trinity making a transition from female to male, defeated Katy Morton Ranch's Chelsea Sanchez.  (Vernon Bryant/The Dallas Morning News)"
          sizes="(min-width: 84.9375em) 905px,
            (min-width: 62em) 65vw,
            88vw">

             <figcaption class="article-content__figure__figcaption secondary-text minion-text--long">
                            <p class="article__figure__attribution"><small>
                    Vernon Bryant/Staff Photographer                </small></p>
                                        <p class="mtm">Euless Trinity's Mack Beggs reacts to winning the state championship title in the girls Class 6A girls 110 weight class during the UIL Wrestling State Tournament at Berry Center in Cypress on Saturday, February 25, 2017. Beggs, a 17-year-old transgender wrestler from Euless Trinity making a transition from female to male, defeated Katy Morton Ranch's Chelsea Sanchez.  (Vernon Bryant/The Dallas Morning News)</p>
                    </figcaption>
    
</figure>
                                    </div>
                                
                            <!--
                             - Embeds
                             -->
                                                    
                                            
                            <!--
                             - Images
                             -->
                                                            
                                <!--
                                 - Basic Content
                                 -->
                                <div class="wysiwyg article-content article-content--text tertia-text--long">
    <p>Beggs' family, wearing red shirts that read "Mack Attack" on the front and "2017 state" plus the person's relationship to Mack in the back, yelled support during a blood timeout.&nbsp;</p><p>Beggs is transitioning from female to male and wants to wrestle boys <a href="http://sportsday.dallasnews.com/high-school/high-schools/2017/02/18/transgender-teen-wins-regional-wrestling-title-despite-attempt-ban-competing">according to his grandmother, but UIL rules won't let him.</a></p><p>Sanchez declined comment.&nbsp;Katy Morton Ranch coach Mark Balser said he was proud of Sanchez in the match but declined to comment further.&nbsp;</p><p>After the match Beggs and Sanchez joked before the awards ceremony. During the ceremony, Beggs counted down and all the place winners dabbed in unison.&nbsp;</p><p>When Beggs' name was announced as champion, only cheers could be heard among the crowd.&nbsp;</p><p>Beggs has been the <a href="http://sportsday.dallasnews.com/high-school/high-schools/2017/02/24/forfeits-euless-trinity-transgender-wrestler-mack-beggs-wins-first-state-tournament-match">subject of controversy and intense media attention all weekend</a>. Coaches, fans, and wrestling parents debated whether Beggs should be allowed to compete after taking testosterone treatments and whether it was fair to the other girls in the competition. Beggs is allowed to compete because he has <a href="http://sportsday.dallasnews.com/high-school/high-schools/2017/02/18/transgender-teen-wins-regional-wrestling-title-despite-attempt-ban-competing">"a valid medical use" to take the testosterone, which is normally a banned steroid.</a></p><p>Arlington Sam Houston's Destiny Dominguez, the state champion at 102 pounds, said she's wrestled Beggs earlier this year and has no problem with Beggs competing.&nbsp;</p><p>"I really think that it's unfair that everybody is so against Mack for this," Dominguez said. "It's nothing strength-wise as a wrestler. It's not how strong you are. It's your mentality, how you wrestle. With Mack, I think it's an inspiration for everybody, despite however many people are against you to be out here and for him to win is such a great thing."&nbsp;</p><p>Dominguez, a senior,&nbsp;said she's&nbsp;wrestled Beggs almost every year and didn't notice a difference in Beggs from the previous years to this year.&nbsp;</p><p>"Mack has always been a tough wrestler," Dominguez said.</p><p>Beggs also&nbsp;defeated&nbsp;Grand Prairie's Kailyn Clay in the state semifinals Saturday morning, winning via fall&nbsp;2:52 into the match.&nbsp;</p></div>
                                                    
                                            
                            <!--
                             - Images
                             -->

                                     - Video
                                     -->

                                            <div class="oo-vid-container" data-oo-content-id="RwNWYxYTE6Gshaf4CeyQfvfaYbj3906Z"></div><script defer src="http://www.dallasnews.com/resources/motif/dist/js/ooyala.js"></script>                                        </figure>
                                    </div>
                                                                                    
                                            
                            <!--
                             - Images
                             -->
                                                            
                                <!--
                                 - Basic Content
                                 -->
                                <div class="wysiwyg article-content article-content--text tertia-text--long">
    <p>After the pin, Beggs' family stood and cheered from the top deck of the stadium. The display was met by a few boos, but seemed to be<a href="http://sportsday.dallasnews.com/high-school/high-schools/2017/02/24/forfeits-euless-trinity-transgender-wrestler-mack-beggs-wins-first-state-tournament-match" target="_blank"> less than what occurred during Beggs' quarterfinal&nbsp;match</a>&nbsp;on Friday.</p><p>Grand Prairie coach Matiana Wiley declined to comment and said that Clay didn't have permission to talk to the media.&nbsp;</p><p>Clay's father didn't have much to say about the matter.</p><p>"She's here to wrestle. That's our comment," Clay's father said before briskly walking away.&nbsp;</p></div>
                                                    
                                            
                            <!--
                             - Images
                             -->
                                                            
                                <!--
                                 - Basic Content
                                 -->
                                <div class="wysiwyg article-content article-content--text tertia-text--long">
    <p>The large contingent of media that followed Beggs on Friday was back again on Saturday, documenting every move.&nbsp;</p><p>Beggs came out of a far entrance onto the floor before his first match of the day&nbsp;and jogged across mats to wrestle. After the match concluded, Beggs showed a little bit of emotion upon reaching the finals before he&nbsp;and his coach, Travis Clark, hurried away from the media scrum and into a restricted area.<br></p><h3 class="align--center">More on Mack Beggs</h3><p><a href="http://sportsday.dallasnews.com/high-school/high-schools/2017/02/25/euless-trinity-transgender-wrestler-mack-beggs-advances-state-finals-meets-boos">Watch complete match videos of Euless Trinity transgender wrestler Mack Beggs' wins at UIL state tournament</a></p><p><a href="http://sportsday.dallasnews.com/high-school/high-schools/2017/02/24/mother-wrestler-lost-trinitys-mack-beggs-match-completely-unfair-win-situation">Mother of wrestler who lost to Euless Trinity's Mack Beggs: Match was 'completely unfair' and 'no-win situation'</a></p><p><a href="http://sportsday.dallasnews.com/high-school/high-schools/2017/02/20/controversy-transgender-wrestler-starts-texas-rules">Controversy over transgender wrestler starts with Texas' rules</a></p><p><a href="http://sportsday.dallasnews.com/high-school/high-schools/2017/02/18/texas-uil-must-create-better-policy-transgender-athletes-higher-court-will">Commentary:&nbsp;Texas, UIL must create better policy for transgender athletes or higher court will</a></p><p><a href="http://sportsday.dallasnews.com/high-school/high-schools/2017/02/20/controversy-transgender-wrestler-starts-texas-rules">Editorial:&nbsp;Texas' shortsighted rules put trans athletes in no-win spot</a></p><p><a href="http://sportsday.dallasnews.com/high-school/high-schools/2017/02/18/transgender-teen-wins-regional-wrestling-title-despite-attempt-ban-competing">Transgender teen wins regional wrestling title despite attempt to ban him from competing</a></p><p><a call Texas UIL birth certificate ruling 'horrible policy' for transgender athletes</a></p></div>
